<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575218 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01852: SvcV-3a Systems-Services Matrix

- page_id: `249575218`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575218/SvcV-3a+Systems-Services+Matrix
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-01-30T15:38:49.642+01:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-3a-systems-services-matrix', 'svcv-3a']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1325408687

1325408690

1325408688

**Description**

A SvcV-3a enables a quick overview of all the system-to-service resource interactions specified in one or more SvcV-1 Services Context Description models. The SvcV-3a provides a tabular summary of the system and services interactions specified in the SvcV-1 Services Context Description for the Architectural Description. This model can be useful in support existing systems that are transitioning to provide services. The matrix format supports a rapid assessment of potential commonalities and redundancies (or, if fault-tolerance is desired, the lack of redundancies).

The SvcV-3a can be organized in a number of ways to emphasize the association of system-to-service interactions in context with the architecture’s purpose.

The intended usage of the SvcV-3a includes:

- Summarizing system and service resource interactions.
- Interface management.
- Comparing interoperability characteristics of solution options.

**Implementation**

SvcV-3a can be represented using a SvcV-3a diagram which is an editable Dependency Matrix.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

The SvcV-3a provides a tabular summary of the system and services interactions specified in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-1 Services Context Description' space='UPDM2P']. Each Resource Interaction listed in the SvcV-3a table should be traceable to Operational Exchange listed in the corresponding [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='OV-3 Operational Resource Flow Matrix' space='UPDM2P']. Each Resource Interaction may relate to a known Function (from [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description' space='UPDM2P']) that produces or consumes it. Exchange Elements as well as the other type of Resource Interaction Items are exchanged by Service Providers and Service Requesters represented in [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-6 Services Resource Flow Matrix' space='UPDM2P'].

1325408685

**Related Pages:**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Service Access' space='UPDM2P']

## PAGE 01853: SvcV-3b Services-Services Matrix

- page_id: `249575222`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575222/SvcV-3b+Services-Services+Matrix
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-01-30T15:35:42.520+01:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-3b-services-services-matrix', 'svcv-3b']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1325727484

1325727487

1325727486

**Description**

A SvcV-3b enables a quick overview of all the services resource interactions specified in one or more SvcV-1 Services Context Description models. The SvcV-3b provides a tabular summary of the services interactions specified in the SvcV-1 Services Context Description for the Architectural Description. The matrix format supports a rapid assessment of potential commonalities and redundancies (or, if fault-tolerance is desired, the lack of redundancies). In addition, this model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services as an input to the SvcV-10a Services Rules Model, SvcV-10b Services State Transition Description, and SvcV-10c Services Event-Trace Description, implemented as orchestrations of services.

The SvcV-3b can be organized in a number of ways to emphasize the association of service pairs in context with the architecture’s purpose. One type of organization is a Service Hierarchy or Taxonomy of Services.

The intended usage of the SvcV-3b includes:

- Summarizing service resource interactions.
- Interface management.
- Comparing interoperability characteristics of solution options.

**Implementation**

SvcV-3b can be represented using a SvcV-3b diagram which is an editable Dependency Matrix.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

This model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services as an input to the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-10a Services Rules Model' space='UPDM2P'], [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-10b Services State Transition Description' space='UPDM2P'], and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-10c Services Event-Trace Description' space='UPDM2P'], implemented as orchestrations of services.

1325727483

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575226 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01854: SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description

- page_id: `249575226`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575226/SvcV-4+Services+Functionality+Description
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-14T11:04:44.397+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-4-services-functionality-description', 'svcv-4']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Description**

The SvcV-4 DoDAF-described Model addresses human and service functionality.

The primary purpose of SvcV-4 is to:

- Develop a clear description of the necessary data flows that are input (consumed) by and output (produced) by each resource.
- Ensure that the service functional connectivity is complete (i.e., that a resource’s required inputs are all satisfied).
- Ensure that the functional decomposition reaches an appropriate level of detail.

The Services Functionality Description provides detailed information regarding the:

- Allocation of service functions to resources.
- Flow of resources between service functions.

The SvcV-4 is the Services Viewpoint counterpart to the OV-5b Operational Activity Model of the Operational Viewpoint.

The intended usage of the SvcV-4 includes:

- Description of task workflow.
- Identification of functional service requirements.
- Functional decomposition of Services.
- Relate human and service functions.

**Implementation**

SvcV-4 can be represented using:

- A SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description diagram which is based on the UML Class diagram. [ATTACHMENT filename='SvcV-4_hierarchy.png']
- A SvcV-4 Services Functionality Flow Description diagram which is based on the UML Activity diagram. [ATTACHMENT filename='SvcV-4_flows.png']

The SvcV-4 is the behavioral counterpart to the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-1 Services Context Description' space='UPDM2P'] (in the same way that [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating OV-5b Operational Activity Flow Model diagram' space='UPDM2P'] is the behavioral counterpart to [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='OV-2 Operational Resource Flow Description' space='UPDM2P']).

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

#### PANEL: Related elements

Related elements

- Function
- Service Access
- Function Action
- Function Edge
- Resource Parameter

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575232 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01855: SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description BPD

- page_id: `249575232`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575232/SvcV-4+Services+Functionality+Description+BPD
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2018-07-12T10:09:50.011+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description (BPD) diagram is based on BPMN Process Diagram (BPD). It describes a sequence or flow of activities in an organization that shows how the businesswork. The diagram shows activities, events, and data that trigger or feed businessactivities.

SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description (BPD) diagram is similar to the BPMN Process Diagram (BPD).

Some diagram elements have both UPDM and BPMN stereotypes.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:layout><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_right_sidebar"><ac:layout-cell><p>SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description (BPD) diagram is based on BPMN Process Diagram (BPD). It describes a sequence or flow of activities in an organization that shows how the <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">business </span>work. The diagram shows activities, events, and data that trigger or feed <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">business </span>activities.</p><p>SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description (BPD) diagram is similar to the BPMN Process Diagram (BPD).</p><p>Some diagram elements have both UPDM and BPMN stereotypes.</p></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><p> </p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section></ac:layout>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575233 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01856: SvcV-5 Operational Activity to Services Traceability Matrix

- page_id: `249575233`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575233/SvcV-5+Operational+Activity+to+Services+Traceability+Matrix
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-14T11:11:37.849+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-5-operational-activity-to-services-traceability-matrix', 'svcv-5']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Description**

The SvcV-5 addresses the linkage between service functions described in SvcV-4 and Operational Activities specified in OV-5a Operational Activity Decomposition Tree or OV-5b Operational Activity Model. The SvcV-5 depicts the mapping of service functions (and, optionally, the capabilities and performers that provide them) to operational activities and thus identifies the transformation of an operational need into a purposeful action performed by a service solution. During requirements definition, the SvcV-5 plays a particularly important role in tracing the architectural elements associated with system function requirements to those associated with user requirements.

The intended usage of the SvcV-5 includes:

- Tracing service functional requirements to user requirements.
- Tracing solution options to requirements.
- Identification of overlaps or gaps.

**Implementation**

SvcV-5 can be represented using a SvcV-5 diagram which is an editable Dependency Matrix. Service Accesses are used as row elements and Operational Activities are used as column elements.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

DoDAF uses the term Operational Activity in the OVs and the term Service Function in the SVs to refer to essentially the same kind of thing—both activities and service functions are tasks that are performed, accept inputs, and develop outputs. The distinction between an Operational Activity and a Service Function is a question of what and how. The Operational Activity is a specification of what is to be done, regardless of the mechanism used. A Service Function specifies how a resource carries it out. For this reason, the SvcV-5 is a significant model, as it ties together the logical specification in the[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating OV-5a Operational Activity Model diagram' space='UPDM2P'] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating OV-5b Operational Activity Flow Model diagram' space='UPDM2P'] with the physical specification of the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description' space='UPDM2P']. Service Functions can be carried out by Resources.

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

#### PANEL: Related elements

Related elements

- Service Access
- Activity Performed By Performer
- Function
- Operational Activity

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE


<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575236 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01857: SvcV-6 Services Resource Flow Matrix

- page_id: `249575236`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575236/SvcV-6+Services+Resource+Flow+Matrix
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-06-18T10:29:19.553+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-6-services-resource-flow-matrix', 'svcv-6']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Description**

The SvcV-6 specifies the characteristics of Service Resource Flow exchanges between Services. The SvcV- is the physical equivalent of the logical OV-3 Operational Resource Flow Matrix and provides detailed information on the service connections which implement the Resource Flow exchanges specified in OV-3 Operational Resource Flow Matrix.

In addition, this model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services. According to the Net-Centric Data Strategy, a net-centric implementation needs to focus in on the data in the Service Resource Flow, as well as the services that produce or consume the data of the Service Resource Flow. In a net-centric implementation, not all the consumers are known and this model emphasizes the focus on the producer and Service Resource Flow.

**Implementation**

SvcV-6 can be represented using:

- A SvcV-6 table.
- An SvcV-6 role-based table. A role-based table represents exchanges between Resource Roles (resource usages).
- A SvcV-6 spreadsheet report.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Each Resource Interaction listed in the SvcV- 6 table should be traceable to Operational Exchange listed in the corresponding [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='OV-3 Operational Resource Flow Matrix' space='UPDM2P']. Each Resource Interaction may relate to a known Function (from [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-4 Services Functionality Description' space='UPDM2P']) that produces or consumes it. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-7 Services Measures Matrix' space='UPDM2P'] builds on the SvcV-6 and should be developed at the same time. Exchange Elements as well as the other type of Resource Interaction Items are exchanged by Service Providers and Service Requesters represented in SvcV-6 table ([CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='DIV-2 Logical Data Model' space='UPDM2P'], [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='DIV-3 Physical Data Model' space='UPDM2P']).

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating SvcV-6 table' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Displaying Custom Measurements' space='UPDM2P']

#### PANEL: Related elements

Related elements

- Service Access
- Resource Interaction
- Exchange Element
- Function
- System
- Software
- Capability Configuration
- Organization Type
- Person Type

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575239 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01858: SvcV-7 Services Measures Matrix

- page_id: `249575239`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575239/SvcV-7+Services+Measures+Matrix
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-14T11:14:48.870+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-7-services-measures-matrix', 'svcv-7']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Description**

The SvcV-7 depicts the measures (metrics) of resources. The Services Measures Matrix expands on the information presented in a SvcV-1 Services Context Description by depicting the characteristics of the resources in the SvcV-1 Services Context Description.

In addition, this model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services. Service measures for Service Level Agreements for each service and may include number of service consumers, service usage by consumers, and the minimum, average and maximum response times, allowed down time, etc. Measures of interest for a Chief Information Office or Program manager may include measures that assess service reuse, process efficiency, and business agility.

The intended usage of the SvcV-7 includes:

- Definition of performance characteristics and measures (metrics).
- Identification of non-functional requirements.

**Implementation**

SvcV-7 can be represented using:

- A SvcV-7 typical measures table. [ATTACHMENT filename='SvcV-7_Typical.PNG']
- A SvcV-7 actual measures table. [ATTACHMENT filename='SvcV-7_Actual.PNG']
- A SvcV-7 actual measures spreadsheet report.

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating SvcV-7 Typical table' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating SvcV-7 Actual table' space='UPDM2P']
- Generating SvcV-7 Actual table from SvcV-7 Typical table
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Generating document based reports' space='UPDM2P']

#### PANEL: Related elements

Related elements

- Service Access
- Measure Type
- Actual Property
- Measure
- Measurement

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575245 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01859: SvcV-8 Services Evolution Description

- page_id: `249575245`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575245/SvcV-8+Services+Evolution+Description
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-17T08:40:57.469+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-8-services-evolution-description', 'svcv-8']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Description**

The SvcV-8 presents a whole lifecycle view of resources (services), describing how it changes over time. It shows the structure of several resources mapped against a timeline.

In addition, this model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services. This model can present a timeline of services evolve or are replaced over time, including services that are internal and external to the scope of the architecture.

The intended usage of the SvcV-8 includes:

- Development of incremental acquisition strategy.
- Planning technology insertion.

**Implementation**

The SvcV-8 view can be represented using a SvcV-8 Services Evolution Description diagram which is realized as a time based diagram.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

#### PANEL: Related elements

Related elements

- Whole Life Configuration
- Version Of Configuration
- Service Access
- System
- Software
- Capability Configuration
- Organization Type
- Person Type
- Actual Project Milestone
- Increment Milestone
- Out Of Service Milestone

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575250 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01860: SvcV-9 Services Technology and Skills Forecast

- page_id: `249575250`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575250/SvcV-9+Services+Technology+and+Skills+Forecast
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-14T11:22:49.554+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views > Services viewpoint
- labels: ['svcv-9-services-technology-and-skills-forecast', 'svcv-9']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Description**

The SvcV-9 defines the underlying current and expected supporting technologies and skills. Expected supporting technologies and skills are those that can be reasonably forecast given the current state of technology and skills, and expected improvements or trends. New technologies and skills are tied to specific time periods, which can correlate against the time periods used in SvcV-8 Services Evolution Description model milestones and linked to Capability Phases.

The SvcV-9 provides a summary of emerging technologies and skills that impact the architecture. The SvcV-9 provides descriptions of relevant:

- Emerging capabilities.
- Industry trends.
- Predictions (with associated confidence factors) of the availability and readiness of specific hardware and software services.
- Current and possible future skills.

In addition to providing an inventory of trends, capabilities and services, the SvcV-9 also includes an assessment of the potential impact of these items on the architecture. Given the future-oriented nature of this model, forecasts are typically made in short, mid and long-term timeframes, such as 6, 12 and 18-month intervals. In addition, this model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services. As technologies change, like incorporation of Representational State Transfer (REST) services in the Web Services Description Language, this model can present a timeline of technologies related services over time.

The intended usage of the SvcV-9 includes:

- Forecasting technology readiness against time.
- HR Trends Analysis.
- Recruitment Planning.
- Planning technology insertion.
- Input to options analysis.

**Implementation**

SvcV-9 can be represented using a SvcV-9 table.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

The specific time periods selected (and the trends being tracked) can be coordinated with architecture transition plans (which the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='SvcV-8 Services Evolution Description' space='UPDM2P'] can support). That is, insertion of new capabilities and upgrading or re-training of existing resources may depend on or be driven by the availability of new technology and associated skills.

If standards are an integral part of the technologies important to the evolution of a given architecture, then it may be convenient to combine SvcV-9 with the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='StdV-2 Standards Forecast' space='UPDM2P'] into a composite Fit-for-Purpose View.

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

#### PANEL: Related elements

Related elements

- Forecast
- Service Access

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:layout><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_right_sidebar"><ac:layout-cell><p><strong>Description</strong></p><p>The SvcV-9 defines the underlying current and expected supporting technologies and skills. Expected supporting technologies and skills are those that can be reasonably forecast given the current state of technology and skills, and expected improvements or trends. New technologies and skills are tied to specific time periods, which can correlate against the time periods used in SvcV-8 Services Evolution Description model milestones and linked to Capability Phases.</p><p>The SvcV-9 provides a summary of emerging technologies and skills that impact the architecture. The SvcV-9 provides descriptions of relevant:</p><ul><li>Emerging capabilities.</li><li>Industry trends.</li><li>Predictions (with associated confidence factors) of the availability and readiness of specific hardware and software services.</li><li>Current and possible future skills.</li></ul><p>In addition to providing an inventory of trends, capabilities and services, the SvcV-9 also includes an assessment of the potential impact of these items on the architecture. Given the future-oriented nature of this model, forecasts are typically made in short, mid and long-term timeframes, such as 6, 12 and 18-month intervals. In addition, this model is useful in support of net-centric (service-oriented) implementation of services. As technologies change, like incorporation of Representational State Transfer (REST) services in the Web Services Description Language, this model can present a timeline of technologies related services over time.</p><p>The intended usage of the SvcV-9 includes:</p><ul><li>Forecasting technology readiness against time.</li><li>HR Trends Analysis.</li><li>Recruitment Planning.</li><li>Planning technology insertion.</li><li>Input to options analysis.</li></ul><p><strong>Implementation</strong></p><p>SvcV-9 can be represented using a SvcV-9 table.</p><p><ac:image ac:alt="SvcV-9 Services Technology and Skills Forecast" ac:title="SvcV-9 Services Technology and Skills Forecast"><ri:attachment ri:filename="SvcV-9.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="SvcV-9 Services Technology and Skills Forecast" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p>The specific time periods selected (and the trends being tracked) can be coordinated with architecture transition plans (which the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="SvcV-8 Services Evolution Description" /></ac:link> can support). That is, insertion of new capabilities and upgrading or re-training of existing resources may depend on or be driven by the availability of new technology and associated skills.</p><p>If standards are an integral part of the technologies important to the evolution of a given architecture, then it may be convenient to combine SvcV-9 with the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="StdV-2 Standards Forecast" /></ac:link> into a composite Fit-for-Purpose View.</p></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><ac:structured-macro ac:macro-id="e650a653-4dcd-42f8-8b6b-0d181c3661f9" ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Related procedures</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><ac:structured-macro ac:macro-id="e508bbff-baac-4438-8da2-ec1ab07e0165" ac:name="children" ac:schema-version="1" /> </p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p> </p><p> </p><p> </p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_equal"><ac:layout-cell><ac:structured-macro ac:macro-id="109d3750-a1c3-4875-bf29-38a3af767fea" ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Related elements</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li>Forecast</li><li>Service Access</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p> </p><p> </p></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><p> </p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section></ac:layout>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575253 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01864: Systems viewpoint

- page_id: `249575253`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575253/Systems+viewpoint
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-17T11:56:26.095+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > DoDAF 2.0 viewpoints and views
- labels: ['systems-viewpoint']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

“The DoDAF-described Models within the Systems Viewpoint describes systems and interconnections providing for, or supporting, DoD functions. DoD functions include both warfighting and business functions. The Systems Models associate systems resources to the operational and capability requirements. These systems resources support the operational activities and facilitate the exchange of information. The Systems DoDAF-described Models are available for support of legacy systems. As architectures are updated, they should transition from Systems to Services and utilize the models within the Services Viewpoint.” [DoDAF V2.0 Volume II]

800700

#### PANEL: Views

Views

##### Description

MODAF/NAF: A ratified and peer-reviewed specification that is used to guide or constrain the architecture. A Standard may be applied to any element in the architecture via the [constrainedItem] property of UML::Constraint (Standard).

DoDAF: Technical standards document specific technical methodologies and practices to design and implement.

##### Architecture Framework

DoDAF

##### Extensions

UML Class

## PAGE 01866: Temporal Part

- page_id: `249575776`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575776/Temporal+Part
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-01-30T15:02:08.571+01:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > UPDM 2.1 Elements > UPDM 2.1 Capability Viewpoint and Strategic Viewpoint Elements
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

917090645

917090648

917090647

##### Description

UPDM Artifact: An EnterprisePhase can be sub-divided into structural and temporal parts. TemporalPart describes the EnterprisePhase elements that have a time based nature.

MODAF/NAF: Asserts that one EnterprisePhase is a temporal part of another.

This means that both EnterprisePhases have the same spatial extent, i.e., this is only a temporal structure (MODAF::EnterpriseTemporalPart).

##### Architecture Framework

DoDAF, MODAF, NAF

##### Extensions

UML Property

##### Related MODAF Views

[MODAF. StV-1 Enterprise Vision](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/UPDM2P190/MODAF.+StV-1+Enterprise+Vision)

##### Related NAF Views

[NCV-1 Capability Vision](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/UPDM2P190/NCV-1+Capability+Vision)

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575968 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01867: Time Periods dialog

- page_id: `249575968`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575968/Time+Periods+dialog
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2018-05-14T16:22:02.037+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > Dialogs
- labels: ['time-periods-dialog']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

**Related Pages**:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating P1 Technology Forecast table' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating A8 Standards Forecast table' space='UPDM2P']
- Creating StdV-2 table
- Creating SvcV-9 table
- Creating SV-9 table

In the UPDM plugin, time periods are used to specify resources for the architecture against a timeline indicating when they are expected to be in use. The **Time Periods** dialog is essential when defining time periods for the **forecast of the resources**. When [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Time Periods dialog' space='UPDM2P'], you need to select a pre-existing timeline or create a new one, specify different time period types, and provide additional required data.

The **Time Periods** dialog consists of three areas:

- **Toolbar** - This area allows you to control how properties are displayed in the dialog.
- **Properties** - Provides the list of all properties that are available to specify.
- Properties value cells - The spaces where you can set values for the properties.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Time periods can be defined when the subjects, or resources, of the forecast are already added in the table. In other words, the **Technology area** column must be filled in with resources before adding a specific time period. Now, it is possible to use the**Time Periods** dialog.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

The steps below show you how to work with the**Time Periods**dialog by explaining all properties that should have values defined, and by showing you how to specify those values.

procedureTo specify time periods using the **Time Periods** dialog

1. Open the **Time Periods** dialog, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] on the table toolbar. [IMAGE alt='' src='']
2. (Optional) If you want to modify the view of listed properties, enable the buttons from the **Time Periods** dialog toolbar:
  - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to group properties by the categories.
  - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to list properties alphabetically.
  - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to expand all collapsed categories.
  - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to collapse all expanded categories.
3. Specify the Timeline property:
  - Select a preexisting Timeline element. How to select an existing TimelineClick on the Timeline property value box, and do one of the following: 
 - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''], or press Alt+Down. 
 - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''], and select it from the opened **Select Timeline** dialog. 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
  - Create a new Timeline element via the dialog. How to create a new Timelinea) Click on the Timeline property value box. 
b) Select [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to open the **Select Timeline** dialog. 
c) Ensure that element **Creation Mode** is turned on. 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
d) Select the appropriate package from the list in which you want to store a new Timeline element. 
e) Click the **Create** button, or, from the shortcut menu of the selected package, select **Create** > **Timeline**. The Specification window of the newly created Timeline opens automatically.[IMAGE alt='' src='']f) Type the name of the new Timeline, and click **Close**. 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
g) In the **Select Timeline** dialog, select the newly created Timeline, and click **OK**. 
The timeline is now selected as a Timeline property value. 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
4. Select one of three Forecast Kinds asproperty values:
  - Periodic - to divide the forecast into equal periods.
  - Specified Dates - to divide the forecast into specific dates.
  - Specified Periods - to divide the forecast into specific time periods. [IMAGE alt='' src='']
5. Specify other properties from the selected Forecast Kind value:
  - 
    - If you selected the Periodic type, you need to define those active properties: 
 - From Date property. To select the date on which the forecast will begin, use one of the following ways: 
- Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] or Press Alt+Down ,and select already existing date from the list. 
 - Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''], and select it from the opened [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Date and Time Settings dialog' space='UPDMP183']**Date and Time Settings** dialog. 
 - Number of Periods property. Type the number of forecast periods. 
 - Period Length property. Type a number specifying the length of the forecast according to Length Unit property. 
 - Length Unit property. Select the unit to use when measuring the length of a forecast: Years, Months, or Days. 
 [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Example of the forecast table (SV-9) with Periodic Forecast KindAll data defined in the**Time Periods** dialog is displayed automatically in columns by diving periods.[IMAGE alt='' src='']
  - If you selected the Specified Dates type, you only need to define the Forecast Dates property value. How to define Forecast Dates property valuea) Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to edit the value cell. The **Select ISO8601 Date Time** dialog opens. 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
 
b) Select the existing ISO8601DateTime element (date) from the **List** , or create a new one.How to create a new ISO8601DateTime (date)a. In the **Select ISO8601 Date Time** dialog, ensurethat element **Creation Mode** is turned on. 
b. Select the appropriate package from the list in which you want to store a new ISO8601DateTime element (date). 
c. Click the **Create** button, or, from the shortcut menu of the selected package, select **Create** > **ISO8601DateTime**. The Specification window of the newly created ISO8601DateTime elementopens automatically. 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
d. Specify the Value property by clicking the [IMAGE alt='' src=''], and selecting an appropriate date from the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Date and Time Settings dialog' space='UPDMP183']**Date and Time Settings** dialog. 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']e. Click **Close,** or create more dates by repeating steps c. and d.c) Click **OK**. [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Example of the forecast table (SV-9) with Specified Dates Forecast KindAll data defined in the **Time Periods** dialog are displayed in columns in the table. In this case, three dates (2016-09-23, 2017-09-23, and 2018-03-23) were automatically divided into two columns (from 2016-09-23 to 2017-09-23, and from 2017-09-23 to 2018-03-23).[IMAGE alt='' src='']
  - If you selected Specified Periods type, you only need to define the Time Periods property value. How to define Time Periods property valuea)Select the Time Periods property value box. 
b) Click[IMAGE alt='' src=''] to edit the value cell.c) In the **Select Time Period** dialog you can: - Double-click to select existing Time Periods ([IMAGE alt='' src='']) one by one from the **List**tab. 
 - Expand an existing Timeline element ([IMAGE alt='' src='']) with time periods defined in the **Tree** tab, and double-click on Time Periods to choose them one by one. 
 - Create a new Timeline element withTime Periods.How to create the Timeline with Time Periodsa. Ensure that element **Creation Mode** is turned on. 
b. Select the appropriate package from the list in which you want to store a new Timeline element. 
c. Click the **Create** button, or, from the shortcut menu of selected package, select **Create** > **Timeline**. The Specification window of the newly created Timeline opens automatically. 
d. Type a name for the new Timeline, and click **Close**. 
e. Select the newly created Timeline element. 
f. Click the **Create** button, and select **Time Period,** or, from the shortcut menu of the selected Timeline, select **Create** > **Time Period**. The Specification window of the newly created Time Period opens automatically. 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
 
g. Type a name for the newly created Time Period. Specify its Start Date and End Date properties. 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
h. Click **Close**. [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Example of the forecast table (SV-9) with Specified Periods Forecast KindAll time periods defined in the **Time Periods** dialog are displayed in the table as columns. In this case, three periods (2016 period, 2017 period, and 2018 period) with their specific start and end dates were defined and displayed as columns in the SV-9 table.[IMAGE alt='' src='']
6. Click **OK**.

After specifying all required data in this dialog, the new columns appear in the table as time periods. The forecast of resources is now planned and divided into required periods. The following figure illustrates the results in a forecast table after specifying periodical time periods in the**Time Periods** dialog.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Use**Time Period****s** dialog to specify Forecast dates and time periods.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To open **Time Periods** dialog

1. Click [IMAGE alt='' src='']in the toolbar. The**Time Periods** dialog opens.

This area allows you to control how properties are displayed in the dialog.</p></li><li><p><strong>Properties</strong> - Provides the list of all properties that are available to specify.</p></li><li><strong>Properties value cells</strong> - The spaces where you can set values for the properties.</li></ul><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);"><ac:image ac:align="center" ac:title="Three main sections of the Time Periods dialog: Toolbar, Properties, and Properties value cells."><ri:attachment ri:filename="areas_in_time_periods_dialog.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Time Periods dialog" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">T</span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">ime periods can be defined when the subjects, or resources, of the forecast are already added in the table. In other words, the <strong>Technology area</strong> column must be filled in with resources before adding a specific time period. Specify the Value property by clicking the <ac:image ac:title="Edit" ac:alt="Edit"><ri:attachment ri:filename="edit_button.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Time Periods dialog" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>, and selecting an appropriate date from the <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDMP183" ri:content-title="Date and Time Settings dialog" /><ac:link-body><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"><strong>Date and Time Settings</strong></span></ac:link-body></ac:link> dialog.</span><br /><ac:image ac:title="After the new ISO8601DateTime element is created, its specific date must be selected from the Date and Time Settings dialog which opens automatically when trying to edit the Value property box." ac:alt="After the new ISO8601DateTime element is created, its specific date must be selected from the Date and Time Settings dialog which opens automatically when trying to edit the Value property box."><ri:attachment ri:filename="specifying_value_property_of_ISO8601DateTime.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Time Periods dialog" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /></span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">e. Click <strong>Close,</strong> or create more dates by repeating steps c. and d.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">c) Click <strong>OK</strong>.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"><ac:image ac:title="When the Forecast Kind property value is Specified Dates, in this case three specific dates of this forecast are defined: 2016-09-23, 2017-09-23, and 2018-03-23. <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249576063 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01868: Traceability relation maps

- page_id: `249576063`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249576063/Traceability+relation+maps
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-06-11T14:55:32.918+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > Procedures > Managing Traceability and Impact Analysis
- labels: ['traceability-relation-maps', 'capability-structural-map', 'capability-behavioral-map', 'implementation-map', 'operational-activity-implementation-map', 'operational-activity-map', 'organization-structure-map', 'system-resource-map', 'variant-map']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

A Relation Map diagram enables you to review and analyze relations rapidly between the elements of the whole model.

The UPDM 2 Plugin presents you a number of predefined relation maps. You will be able to change the context and scope only.

You can change the context by dragging the selected element onto the map.

The predefined relation maps are the following:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Traceability relation maps' space='UPDM2P']

**StructuralCapability Structural Map**

A Capability Structural Map depicts the structural relationships of a Capability. The predefined map includes:

- the Capability itself
- related DoDAF Performers (or MODAF Nodes)
- related concrete System Resources including Capability Configurations, Organization Types, Software System Resources

A Capability Structural Map also presents the internal compositions of each mapped element as well as the relationships among these elements.

**BehavioralCapability Behavioral Map**

A Capability Behavioral Map depicts the behavioral relationships of a Capability. The predefined map includes:

- the Capability itself
- related Operational Activities
- related System Functions

A Capability Behavioral Map also presents the internal decomposition of each mapped behavioral element as well as the relationships among these elements.

****

**ImplementationImplementation Map**

The Implementation Map depicts the implementation relationships of a DoDAF Performer (or of a MODAF Node). The predefined map includes either the DoDAF Performer (or the MODAF Node) and the concrete System Resource(s) that has (have) been indicated as implementing that operational element. For example, the Capability Configuration, Organization Type, or Software element that implements the Performer or Node. When the Performer or Node has composite structure and when the System Resources have composite structure, the Implementation Map also includes the implementation elements for the composed elements.

**Activity_ImplementationOperational Activity Implementation Map**

The Operational Activity Implementation Map depicts the behavioral implementation of an Operational Activity, relating the Operational Activity and the Systems Functions that implement the operational behavior. When the Operational Activity has composite behaviors and when the System Functions have composite functionality, the Operational Activity Implementation Map also includes the behavioral elements for the composed elements.

**Operational_ActivityOperational Activity Map**

The Operational Activity Map depicts the behavioral decomposition of an Operational Activity.

**OrganizationOrganization Structure Map**

The Organization Structure Map depicts the structural composition of an Actual Organization. The predefined map includes: the Actual Organization itself, DoDAF Individual Person Roles (or MODAF Actual Posts), and Actual Person elements. The Organization Structure Map illustrates the relationships between these organizational elements.

**SystemSystem Resource Map**

The System Resource Map depicts the structural decomposition of a concrete System Resource-such as a Capability Configuration, Organization Type, or Software-element.

**VariantVariant Map**

The Variant Map depicts concrete specializations of an abstract System Resource such as the direct specializations Service Access, Capability Configuration, and Software and any other specializations of these that appear in the modeled generalization hierarchy.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Related procedures

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249575847 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01869: Trustline

- page_id: `249575847`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249575847/Trustline
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-01-30T15:34:39.281+01:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > UPDM 2.1 Elements > UPDM 2.1 Operational Viewpoint Elements
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1101099757

1101099759

1101099758

##### Description

MODAF/NAF: Asserts that the trustingParty (either a Node or a KnownResource) trusts the trustedParty to a given level (indicated by the level attribute).

No unit of measure is associated with the level - security architects must define their own scale of trust levels for a given architecture or set of architectures.

DoDAF: NA

##### Architecture Framework

MODAF, NAF

##### Properties

| Property | Description |
| --- | --- |
| level : String | String denoting the level of Trust in the information source |

##### Extensions

UML Dependency

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

## PAGE 01870: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation

- page_id: `249575090`

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249576094 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01880: Using Expand/Collapse Internal Structure Compartment

- page_id: `249576094`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249576094/Using+Expand+Collapse+Internal+Structure+Compartment
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-05-27T14:11:31.870+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > Procedures
- labels: ['expand-internal-structure-compartment', 'collapse-internal-structure-compartment']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The **Expand / Collapse internal structure compartment** functionality is available from the element’s smart manipulator toolbar.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

If you have an internal structure defined for the selected element, after clicking the Expand internal structure compartment button the compartment is expanded and the existing internal structure is displayed in it.

If you have more that one internal structure defined, none of them are displayed in the expanded compartment after clicking the **Expand internal structure compartment** button.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE


<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249576076 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01881: Using Libraries

- page_id: `249576076`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249576076/Using+Libraries
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-05-27T11:41:14.400+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > Procedures
- labels: ['libraries', 'universal-joint-task-list', 'ujtl', 'dod-it-standards-registry', 'disr', 'joint-conditions-library', 'add-standard-policy-from-disr-library']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

UPDM 2 plugin supports three element libraries:

1. The Universal Joint Task List (UJTL).
2. DoD Information Technology Standards and Profile Registry (DISR).
3. Joint Conditions.

The **Universal Joint Task List (UJTL)**, when augmented with the Service task lists, is a comprehensive integrated menu of functional tasks, conditions, measures, and criteria. It supports all levels of the Department of Defense in executing the National Military Strategy. In UPDM UJTL library consists of a list of Operational Activities representing universal joint tasks.

The **DoD IT Standards Registry (DISR)** is an online repository of IT standards formerly captured in the Joint Technical Architecture (JTA), Version 6.0. DISR replaces JTA. In UPDM, DISR is the list of standard elements that any of UPDM element may conform to. DISR Library usage is the same as UJTL library. Library item indexes are included when searching for elements within the element Selection dialog.

The **Joint Conditions Library** supports physical, military, and civil locations, where joint tasks can be performed.You can use it, when selecting Locations.

**Case Study**

Let us say, we need to add a standard or a policy for a system element using the StdV-1 Standards Profile table. We will select a standard from the DISR library.

To add a standard/policy from the DISR library

1. Create the StdV-1 diagram.
2. Create new or add an existing system element.
3. In the Standard / Policy cell of the created or added row, click the Edit button. The Select Standard dialog opens.
4. Click the DISR Library tab. The list of DISR standards is displayed.
5. Select the standard and do one of the following:
  - Double-click the selected standard to add it to the Selected elements list.
  - Click the + button to add the selected standard to the Selected elements list.
6. Click OK , after you finish selecting the standards.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:layout><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_right_sidebar"><ac:layout-cell><p>UPDM 2 plugin supports three element libraries:</p><ol><li>The Universal Joint Task List (UJTL).</li><li>DoD Information Technology Standards and Profile Registry (DISR).</li><li>Joint Conditions.</li></ol><p>The <strong>Universal Joint Task List (UJTL)</strong>, when augmented with the Service task lists, is a comprehensive integrated menu of functional tasks, conditions, measures, and criteria. <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249576078 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
````
## PAGE 01882: Using SysML Compliance Mode

- page_id: `249576078`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249576078/Using+SysML+Compliance+Mode
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-05-27T12:51:49.626+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > Procedures
- labels: ['sysml-compliance-mode']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can use SysML capabilities in your UPDM model. For that purpose you can enable the SysML compliance mode in one of the following ways:

- Enable the SysML compliance mode while creating a new project.
- Enable the SysML compliance mode after the project is created.

To enable SysML compliance mode while creating a new project

1. Click File > New Project . The New Project dialog opens.
2. Select project template, specify its name, and location.
3. In the <project template> Project Options area, set the SysML compliance mode (UPDM L1 compliance level) property value to true .
4. Click OK , when you are done.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To turn on SysML compliance mode after the project is created

1. Click Options > Project . The Project Options dialog opens.
2. Select General > UPDM .
3. In the **UPDM** property group, set the **SysML compliance mode (UPDM L1 compliance level)** property value to *true*. You can use the Quick filter box to find the **SysML compliance mode (UPDM L1 compliance level)** property more quickly. Simply start typing the property name in the Quick filter box.
4. Click OK .

When the SysML compliance mode is turned on, control flows are represented as dashed line in activity based diagrams. You can change the representation style to the solid line.

To change the representation to the solid line

1. Click Options > Project . The Project Options dialog opens.
2. Select General > UPDM .
3. In the **UPDM** properties group, set the **Display solid control flows in SysML compliance mode** property value to *true*. You can use the Quick filter box to find the **Display solid control flows in SysML compliance mode** property more quickly. Simply start typing the property name in the Quick filter box.
4. Click **OK**.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

**Case Study**

The following example describes the actual situation, how you can use the SysML compliance mode in the UPDM model.

Let us say, we need to describe a full-time equivalent (FTE) calculations in the UPDM model.

First, we need to create the typical organizational structure using OV-4 Organizational Relationship Chart diagram. The typical organizational structure defines types of departments and roles and how they are associated together in the modeled enterprise. The Department can contain any number of Employees and any number of sub Departments.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Secondly, we generate an actual organizational chart based on the typical organizational chart (see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Instantiating Structures' space='UPDM2P']). An actual organizational chart shows concrete departments and residing employees.

Each employee works a certain number of FTEs.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Thirdly, we can use the SysML Parametric Diagram to describe the recursive FTE’s calculation for the selected department and each residing sub-department.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

You can execute the described calculations using Cameo Simulation Toolkit.

#### PANEL: Related procedures

Related procedures

The <strong>New Project</strong> dialog opens.</li><li>Select project template, specify its name, and location.</li><li>In the <strong>&lt;project template&gt; Project Options</strong> area, set the <strong>SysML compliance mode (UPDM L1 compliance level)</strong> property value to <em>true</em>.</li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong>, when you are done.</li></ol><p><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="sysml_comliance_mode_property.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Using SysML Compliance Mode" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p> </p><p>To turn on SysML compliance mode after the project is created</p><hr /><ol><li>Click <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Project</strong>. The <strong>Project Options</strong> dialog opens.</li><li>Select <strong>General</strong> &gt; <strong>UPDM</strong>.</li><li><p>In the <strong>UPDM</strong> property group, set the <strong>SysML compliance mode (UPDM L1 compliance level)</strong> property value to <em>true</em>.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info"><ac:rich-text-body><p>You can use the Quick filter box to find the <strong>SysML compliance mode (UPDM L1 compliance level)</strong> property more quickly. Simply start typing the property name in the Quick filter box.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong>.</li></ol><p>When the SysML compliance mode is turned on, control flows are represented as dashed line in activity based diagrams. You can change the representation style to the solid line.</p><p>To change the representation to the solid line</p><hr /><ol><li>Click <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Project</strong>. The <strong>Project Options</strong> dialog opens.</li><li>Select <strong>General</strong> &gt; <strong>UPDM</strong>.</li><li><p>In the <strong>UPDM</strong> properties group, set the <strong>Display solid control flows in SysML compliance mode</strong> property value to <em>true</em>.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info"><ac:rich-text-body><p>You can use the Quick filter box to find the <strong>Display solid control flows in SysML compliance mode</strong> property more quickly. Simply start typing the property name in the Quick filter box.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong>.</p></li></ol><p><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="sysml_compliance_mode_property_in_project_options_dialog.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Using SysML Compliance Mode" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p> </p><p><strong>Case Study</strong></p><p>The following example describes the actual situation, how you can use the SysML compliance mode in the UPDM model.</p><p>Let us say, we need to describe a full-time equivalent (FTE) calculations in the UPDM model.</p><p>First, we need to create the typical organizational structure using OV-4 Organizational Relationship Chart diagram. The typical organizational structure defines types of departments and roles and how they are associated together in the modeled enterprise. The Department can contain any number of Employees and any number of sub Departments.</p><p><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="OV-4 Typical.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Using SysML Compliance Mode" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p>Secondly, we generate an actual organizational chart based on the typical organizational chart (see <ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Instantiating Structures" /></ac:link>). An actual organizational chart shows concrete departments and residing employees.</p><p>Each employee works a certain number of FTEs.</p><p><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="ActualStructure_CountingFTEs.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Using SysML Compliance Mode" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p>Thirdly, we can use the SysML Parametric Diagram to describe the recursive FTE’s calculation for the selected department and each residing sub-department.</p><p><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="ParametricCounting FTEs.png"><ri:page ri:space-key="UPDM2P" ri:content-title="Using SysML Compliance Mode" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info"><ac:rich-text-body><p>You can execute the described calculations using Cameo Simulation Toolkit.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Related procedures</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p> <ac:structured-macro ac:name="children" /></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section></ac:layout>

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=249576084 space=UPDM2P version=1 -->
## PAGE 01883: Using SysML elements in UPDM 2 plugin

- page_id: `249576084`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249576084/Using+SysML+elements+in+UPDM+2+plugin
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2015-07-16T11:50:37.781+02:00`
- ancestors: UPDM 2 Plugin Documentation > Procedures > Using SysML Compliance Mode
- labels: ['expand-sysml-toolbars', 'use-sysml-elements-in-updm-2-plugin']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

SysML elements can be used to extend UPDM provided set of concepts.

SysML toolbars are available in the following diagrams:

| Icon | View |
| --- | --- |
|  |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |
|  | StV-1 |
|  |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |

SysML toolbars are collapsed by default.

To expand SysML toolbars

1. Click Options > Environment .
2. In the Environment Options dialog, click the UPDM property group.
3. Set the System Engineer User Interface Mode property value to true .
4. Click OK .

****

**Case Study**

We will use the Requirement element, which is a SysML element, in an OV-2 diagram.

Do the following

1. Create an OV-2 diagram.
2. Create a Performer/ Node in the diagram.
3. On the SysML Requirements Diagram toolbar, click the Requirement button.
4. Create a Requirement in the diagram pane.
5. Create the Satisfy relationship between the Performer/ Node and the Requirement.

As you can see in the following figure, we have expressed that the architecture element satisfies the Requirement.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

917121858

917121860

917121859

##### Description

An end that describes the future state of the enterprise, without regard to how it is to be achieved; a mental image of what the future will or could be like.

##### Architecture Framework

DoDAF

##### Properties

| Property | Description |
| --- | --- |
| statement : VisionStatement[*] | A description of the Vision. |
| enterprisePhase : EnterprisePhase[1] | The phase which temporally locates the Vision. |

##### Extensions

UML Class

##### Related DoDAF Views

[CV-1 Vision](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/UPDM2P/CV-1+Vision)

## PAGE 01890: Working With Predefined Metric Suites

- page_id: `249576099`
- space_key: `UPDM2P`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/UPDM2P/pages/249576099/Working+With+Predefined+Metric+Suites

- labels: ['create-metric-table', 'show-metric-suites', 'hide-metric-suites', 'calculate-new-metric', 'recalculate', 'add-new-metric-with-different-parameters', 'show-abbreviation-in-column-name']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

In order to start calculating metrics, first you need to create the metric table.

To create a metric table

1. In the Containment tree, right-click a package which will be a metric parameter.
2. From the shortcut menu, select **Tools** > **Metrics** > **New Metric Table**. [ATTACHMENT filename='Create_metric_table.png']
3. Define a table name, change the table owner (if needed), and select one or more desired metric suites.
4. Click **OK**, when you are done. [ATTACHMENT filename='metric_table.png']

The names of the columns can be abbreviated. If you need to change the column names to abbreviations, in the metric table toolbar, click the **Options** button and select the **Show Abbreviation in Column Name**option.

When you have used more than one metric suite, you can hide some metric suites in the table that are not relevant at that time.

To show or hide metric suites in the metric table

1. In the metric table toolbar, click the Show Metric Suites button.
2. Select the metric suites you want to show or hide.

There are three actions with the metrics. You can:

- Calculate New Metric . Select to calculate a new set of metrics using the parameters of the selected rows. Results of the calculation are added to the table.
- Recalculate . Select to recalculate the set of metrics in the selected row with the same parameters.
- Add New Metric with Different Parameters . Select to add a new metric to the table with copied parameters. Then change the parameters and recalculate the metrics.
